This is super cool. And Iâ€™m glad your brother got this cat. Iâ€™m glad this cat got your brother. But just a reminder to everyone, you can adopt kittens from the shelter for between $40-$100. Every December our local shelter does a thing where you can get two cats for the adoption fee on one. We went and adopted a cat last year in December and decided not to get a second one for free since we didnâ€™t know how our older cat would react to just one, but we hope to get another kitten soon. Usually most shelters in December do drastically reduced adoption costs and often sometimes free adoptions (though they do that less now due to too many people adopting for free then regretting it and the animals ending up stray or back in shelters). But you can also adopt free kittens from local listings. This keeps kittens out of shelters, just try not to support purposeful breeding.

Something I did to work on my cat's comfortableness with me when I first got her was I trained her to like bell rubs, at least from me.  How I did it, was I'd play games with her, the mice/lazer pointers/etc, and whenever she "caught" it, I'd stop, gently roll her over to her side, then stroke her belly. After about a week, she started rolling over onto her back on her own whenever she'd catch things and now sometimes she'll flop down on the floor or bed and wait forever for me to come and pet her.    She's 2 years old now, and she's my precious baby <333   Edit: this doesn't work with all cats, obviously but it's worth a try for Cali. The goal is to lower the aggression over their sensitive stomachs and to trust that you won't hurt them.

This is really cute <3 just one thing, in my opinion pets should cost a LOT more, this is a good way to make SURE you really want that pet and won't change your mind, remember it's not just a toy or cute thing to buy, it's a living thing and an investment in its health and longevity. You're also gonna need a vet and to buy shots and regular checkups and save up for any possible emergencies or illnesses. If it's hard to afford the money to buy the pet initially, sadly that's probably a sign that you're not financially prepared for the next decade (approximately) of cat ownership because it can get expensive. Even rats who can cost as little as 20 or 40 dollars, could rack up vet bills of hundreds or thousands if something comes up, never expect any pet to be cheap in any sense, they're a time and financial commitment, just please remember that.

I personally would have done the research before, but you already adopted them. not trying to send hate, but just suggestions :D heres some things about all cats:   learn cat tail language (this tells you how your cat feels immediately) you can search up images of cat tail language charts and compare the tail your new cat has to the ones on the chart.  donâ€™t look your cat directly in the eye (if you stare them down, they will think itâ€™s aggressive) if you want to look at how cute they are, I suggest to blink rapidly while making eye contact.   you can also tell how your cat feels by looking at their pupils. the bigger they are, the more scared they are. the smaller, the more calm and relaxed. (edit: if they are playing or being playful, their pupils will also be large)  please do not touch you catâ€™s tail or belly. (edit: some people say their cats donâ€™t mind belly rubs. so I just suggest that you make sure the cat really trusts you before you try doing it :>) an example is if you have gained their trust, and they show you their belly, they are trusting you not to touch it. itâ€™s their most vulnerable spot on their body.   I have never owned a pet before (except for a fish but that was when I was 5) and have been doing cat research for years. to anyone who may or may not use this information, thank you for reading :D  *edit: please read everyones replies and maybe ask them instead. im not exactly a professional lol also learned a lot from reading them, so thanks :D*
